## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the rate of change of concentration (dA/dt) as a function of time and concentration in a chemical reaction. This is a classic chemical kinetics problem where the rate law relates the reaction rate to the concentration of reactants, possibly with time-dependent effects.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Zero-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0', 'scenario': 'Reaction rate independent of concentration'}
- {'name': 'First-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to concentration (radioactive decay, unimolecular reactions)'}
- {'name': 'Second-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to square of concentration (bimolecular reactions)'}
- {'name': 'nth-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1', 'scenario': 'General power-law rate expression for arbitrary reaction order'}
- {'name': 'Mixed-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Competing first and second order reaction pathways'}
- {'name': 'Reversible first-order reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1', 'scenario': 'First-order forward and reverse reactions approaching equilibrium'}
- {'name': 'Autocatalytic reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A)', 'scenario': 'Product catalyzes its own formation, logistic-type kinetics'}
- {'name': 'Saturation kinetics (substrate inhibition)', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2)', 'scenario': 'Enzyme kinetics with substrate inhibition at high concentrations'}
- {'name': 'Consecutive reaction rate', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * exp(c2 * t)', 'scenario': 'Concentration change involving intermediate species with exponential time dependence'}
- {'name': 'Power-law with offset', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2', 'scenario': 'General rate law with constant source or sink term'}
- {'name': 'Third-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**3', 'scenario': 'Trimolecular or termolecular reaction rate'}
- {'name': 'Time-dependent rate coefficient', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A', 'scenario': 'First-order kinetics with time-varying rate constant (e.g., temperature ramp)'}
- {'name': 'Fractional order with equilibrium', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * (A - c1)**c2', 'scenario': 'Rate law approaching equilibrium concentration with fractional order'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative rate of change (consumption) → dA_dt typically has a negative leading coefficient when A is a reactant being consumed
- Concentration approaching equilibrium → Rate expression includes (A - A_eq) terms where A_eq is the equilibrium concentration
- Integer reaction orders → Power-law exponents of A are often integers (1, 2, 3) corresponding to molecularity
- Autocatalytic behavior (rate peaks at intermediate concentration) → Product of A and (c - A) terms
- Rate independent of time explicitly → dA/dt depends only on A, not on t directly, in elementary rate laws
- Parallel reaction pathways → Sum of multiple power-law terms in A with different exponents
- Conservation constraints → Rate expressions may embed stoichiometric relationships like (c - A) representing other species
- Approach to steady state → Rate expression that vanishes at specific A values (roots of the rate law)
